<span id="freeTextContainer3223960568905904020">Okay, so the George R. R. Martin intro sold me a little, as he credits this with some of the inspiration for A Song of Ice and Fire. This is the first novel of a series of seven, I believe, written in French and begun in the 1950s, and dealing with the Hundred Years War between France and England. It is interesting to pick up on the elements that Martin borrowed for his own series (the litany of names that the Templar Jacques de Molay repeatedly utters to remind himself of those who have wronged</span>
  <span id="freeText3223960568905904020" style="display:none">Okay, so the George R. R. Martin intro sold me a little, as he credits this with some of the inspiration for A Song of Ice and Fire. This is the first novel of a series of seven, I believe, written in French and begun in the 1950s, and dealing with the Hundred Years War between France and England. It is interesting to pick up on the elements that Martin borrowed for his own series (the litany of names that the Templar Jacques de Molay repeatedly utters to remind himself of those who have wronged him is echoed in Arya Stark's similar repetition of the names of those whom she wishes to see dead) but The Accursed Kings is fascinating in its own right, and - hey - each book is probably less than a third as long as any of Martin's!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3223960568905904020" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1669227104" />
    <a title="Nadine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3759963-nadine"><img alt="Nadine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1566849081p2/3759963.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1669227104?book_show_action=true">Jun 15, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nadine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nadine" href="/user/show/3759963-nadine">Nadine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007491261" href="/book/show/27999638-the-iron-king">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1669227104" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12005801283825558687">The Iron King, dubbed the original Game of Thrones by George R R Martin, follows Philip the Fair at the end of the final trial for the powerful Knights of the Templar. <br/><br/>I'm guilty of reading this because of George R R Martin. The wait for The Winds of Winter is proving to be more difficult than I thought so I grabbed the next best thing. <br/><br/>Throughout the entire book you can clearly see the parallels to A Song of Ice and Fire. I may have read too much into some smaller details, but it was nonetheles</span>
  <span id="freeText12005801283825558687" style="display:none">The Iron King, dubbed the original Game of Thrones by George R R Martin, follows Philip the Fair at the end of the final trial for the powerful Knights of the Templar. <br /><br />I'm guilty of reading this because of George R R Martin. The wait for The Winds of Winter is proving to be more difficult than I thought so I grabbed the next best thing. <br /><br />Throughout the entire book you can clearly see the parallels to A Song of Ice and Fire. I may have read too much into some smaller details, but it was nonetheless fun and exciting to see hints of ASOIAF sprinkled throughout. <br /><br />With any historical fiction novel you have to go into the book with a bit of knowledge of the time period to really enjoy the story. There were many times I had to refer to the character list and timeline at the beginning of the book to situate myself in the story. So I advise future readers to watch a documentary about Philip the Fair before reading. <br /><br />Overall, the story was full of intrigue, mystery, and murder. I would definitely recommend this book to fans of ASOIAF and fantasy readers (since historical fiction and fantasy are almost sister genres). </span>
  <a data-text-id="12005801283825558687" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2287178729" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2287178729" />
    <a title="Roman Clodia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56111743-roman-clodia"><img alt="Roman Clodia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464021031p2/56111743.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2287178729?book_show_action=true">Feb 08, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Roman Clodia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Roman Clodia" href="/user/show/56111743-roman-clodia">Roman Clodia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18963069-the-iron-king">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2287178729" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7794174849149703310"><b>'Power is a bitter thing'</b><br/><br/>An eminently readable historical novel, the first of seven, retelling the story of the Capet dynasty in medieval France. This first book follows Philippe IV (Philip the Fair) from his suppression of the Templars to his death in 1314.<br/><br/>The book was originally published in 1955 and there is a slightly old-fashioned air to the narrative. It reminds me a little of Dumas but without the swashbuckling and sense of humour, especially his La Reine Margot, though this is lighter on</span>
  <span id="freeText7794174849149703310" style="display:none"><b>'Power is a bitter thing'</b><br /><br />An eminently readable historical novel, the first of seven, retelling the story of the Capet dynasty in medieval France. This first book follows Philippe IV (Philip the Fair) from his suppression of the Templars to his death in 1314.<br /><br />The book was originally published in 1955 and there is a slightly old-fashioned air to the narrative. It reminds me a little of Dumas but without the swashbuckling and sense of humour, especially his La Reine Margot, though this is lighter on atmosphere. Druon moves between the machinations of the court and the sexual intrigues of his three daughters-in-law, though both are always seen as political.<br /><br />There are some simplicities in language (they are there in the original French so it's not merely a translation issue) but this is historically detailed to compensate. What it's not is a version of the Philippa Gregory historical romance with modern personalities dressed up in medieval costume. Thankfully! <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7794174849149703310" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_613148923" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/613148923" />
    <a title="Nermin " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12267903-nermin"><img alt="Nermin " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578564696p2/12267903.jpg" /></a>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/613148923?book_show_action=true">May 11, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nermin " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nermin " href="/user/show/12267903-nermin">Nermin </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Nermin  by: </span>
      George R.R. Martin :P
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12267903-nermin?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12267903-nermin?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12267903-nermin?shelf=world-literature">world-literature</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer613148923" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14185524399619976590">Like many people, I decided to pick this up after GRRM's recommendation. In one of his blog post he calles this book the 'original Game of Thrones'. Well, I could spot some similarities but despite it and GRMM's claims, I really don't think A Song of Ice and Fire resembles this book. So if you pick this up expecting another GoT, you may be slightly disappointed. <br/><br/>But just like A song of Ice and fire series, this book is full of court intrigues, betrayals, gruesome executions and sex sex sex. Need</span>
  <span id="freeText14185524399619976590" style="display:none">Like many people, I decided to pick this up after GRRM's recommendation. In one of his blog post he calles this book the 'original Game of Thrones'. Well, I could spot some similarities but despite it and GRMM's claims, I really don't think A Song of Ice and Fire resembles this book. So if you pick this up expecting another GoT, you may be slightly disappointed. <br /><br />But just like A song of Ice and fire series, this book is full of court intrigues, betrayals, gruesome executions and sex sex sex. Needless to say, I love reading about this things and I love historical fiction. So I ended up enjoying this book much more than I thought I would when I started it. It was a surprisingly light, funny and compelling read and I can't wait to lay my hands on the second book of the series!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14185524399619976590" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessie  (Ageless Pages Reviews)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessie  (Ageless Pages Reviews)" href="/user/show/4863162-jessie-ageless-pages-reviews">Jessie  (Ageless Pages Reviews)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4863162-jessie-ageless-pages-reviews?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4863162-jessie-ageless-pages-reviews?shelf=2013-reads">2013-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4863162-jessie-ageless-pages-reviews?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4863162-jessie-ageless-pages-reviews?shelf=reviews-2013">reviews-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4863162-jessie-ageless-pages-reviews?shelf=edelweiss-arc">edelweiss-arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4863162-jessie-ageless-pages-reviews?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4863162-jessie-ageless-pages-reviews?shelf=owned-copy">owned-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4863162-jessie-ageless-pages-reviews?shelf=hf-england">hf-england</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4863162-jessie-ageless-pages-reviews?shelf=royal-family-tiffs-and-squabbles">royal-family-tiffs-and-squabbles</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4863162-jessie-ageless-pages-reviews?shelf=hf-france">hf-france</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer560397458" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2181127959833967037"><b>Read <a href='http://agelesspagesreviews.blogspot.com/2013/03/review-iron-king-by-maurice-druon.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>This Review</a> & More Like It <a href='http://agelesspagesreviews.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>On My Blog</a>!</b><br/><br/>A fascinating look at the events during the reign of France's Philip IV, and which directly led to the Hundred Years War between England and France. A bit dry, but long on detail and intrigue, and with an impressively large cast, <i>The Iron King</i>'s influence on later novels, across genres, is undeniable. Widely read and recognized, Druon's epic work has been published and republished in the 50 years since it first came to be, but its story is as fresh and </span>
  <span id="freeText2181127959833967037" style="display:none"><b>Read <a href="http://agelesspagesreviews.blogspot.com/2013/03/review-iron-king-by-maurice-druon.html" rel="nofollow noopener">This Review</a> &amp; More Like It <a href="http://agelesspagesreviews.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">On My Blog</a>!</b><br /><br />A fascinating look at the events during the reign of France's Philip IV, and which directly led to the Hundred Years War between England and France. A bit dry, but long on detail and intrigue, and with an impressively large cast, <i>The Iron King</i>'s influence on later novels, across genres, is undeniable. Widely read and recognized, Druon's epic work has been published and republished in the 50 years since it first came to be, but its story is as fresh and fascinating as ever. Anyone who enjoys descriptive and detailed historical fiction about France, England and the Hundred Years' War will find a lot to enjoy here.<br /><br />Much has been made of its particular impact on the popular fantasy world of George R. R. Martin's <i>A Song of Ice and Fire series</i> (or <i>A Game of Thrones</i> if you're solely a fan of the tv show). Spanning seven volumes, with a large, disparate cast - from kings to bankers to heretics - the numerous parallels between Druon and Martin's work are easy to spot. While there are (sadly) no dragons to be found in <i>the Iron King</i>, there are she-wolves, betrayals, family curses, torture, court intrigue, and ambition to keep things interesting. Historical fiction is at its best when it makes you curious about the people and times portrayed, and Maurice Druon captures these particular times and these complex people so well, it's hard not to be inquisitive about them once the novel is over.<br /><br /><i>A Game of Thrones</i> has rival families: The Starks and the Lannisters. <i>The Iron King</i> has the royal rival families of the French Capets and the English Plantagenets. George R. R. Martin wasn't lying when he said his Starks and Lannisters had nothing on the Capets and Plantagenets. Both families are filled with fools, ambitious men, capable and deceptive women, and more. While the first Accursed Kings book lacks the amount of sheer drama that <i>A Game of Thrones</i> packs into one novel, it is admittedly much shorter (by hundreds of pages!). But, thankfully, the author manages to infuse those too-short 275 with enough machinations and manipulations to make Littlefinger himself proud.<br /><br /><i>A Game of Thrones</i> has the stalwart and rigidly serious Ned Stark. <i>The Iron King</i> has the severe and authoritarian <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philip_IV_of_France" rel="nofollow noopener">Philip "the Fair" IV of France</a>. Both men are descended from a noble and respected lineage (Ned - Brandon the Builder; Philip - <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_IX_of_France" rel="nofollow noopener">Saint Louis aka Louis IX of France</a>) and both take their responsibilities as leaders very seriously. The comparisons between the two are inevitable for those that have read both works, and it's easy to see how Ned was inspired (and improved upon) Druon's French king. Ned is easier to like, and more personable than the more remote and dispassionate Philip, but they are two men cut from the same cloth.<br /><br /><i>A Game of Thrones</i> has a family matriarch with steel and determination in Catelyn Tully. <i>The Iron King</i> has <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Isabella_of_France" rel="nofollow noopener">Isabella, She-Wolf of France</a> (and reigning Queen of England with <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edward_II" rel="nofollow noopener">Edward II</a>). You may know her best (and inaccurately) as William Wallace's weepy lover in the 1995 movie <a href="http://www.imdb.com/title/tt0112573/" rel="nofollow noopener">Braveheart</a>, but that film does her character a disservice. Cold, calculating, and highly intelligent, Isabella and her actions have more of an impact on the history of two countries than one would guess. Much like Catelyn, Isabella has goals and ambitions of her own - for her children, she will start a war that will kill thousands of people before it is all said and done. Both Isabella and Catelyn are remote and hard to like and can be traced as the initiators of huge struggles, but each are thoroughly fascinating to read.<br /><br /><i>A Game of Thrones</i> has Cersei Lannister, a woman determined to have the love she wants regardless of the constraints society - and marriage - would put upon her. <i>The Iron King</i> has <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Margaret_of_Burgundy,_Queen_of_France" rel="nofollow noopener">Marguerite of Burgundy</a>, who, like Cersei, is unfaithful (and eventually found out) to her royal husband, which casts the paternity and thus the rights of her children in serious doubt and helps set off the series of dynastic disputes. <b>SPOILER for later ASOIAF novels</b>: And, like the Lannister lioness, Marguerite finds herself imprisoned against her will, without hope of freedom or redemption. Cersei may be easier to label as outright evil rather than selfish and short-sighted, but the similarities between the two women are apparent.<br /><br /><i>A Song of Ice and Fire</i> is set to be published in a series of seven novels. Druon's series The Accursed Kings is a seven volume work. They are hard to come across, especially in English, but Harper Collins seems to be in the long process of republishing them in 2013. I, for one, am eagerly awaiting the day I can continue this series and see how it all plays out in Druon's version of the Hundred Year's War.<br /><br />The story that has begun to unfold here in the first novel continues in book two, <i>The Strangled Queen</i>. If it is anything like its predecessor I will be a big fan.<br /><br /><b>Happy Game of Thrones day, everyone!</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="2181127959833967037" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_3328236382" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3328236382" />
    <a title="Ozymandias" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22223147-ozymandias"><img alt="Ozymandias" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1373892974p2/22223147.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3328236382?book_show_action=true">May 11, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ozymandias" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ozymandias" href="/user/show/22223147-ozymandias">Ozymandias</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22223147-ozymandias?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22223147-ozymandias?shelf=fiction-medieval">fiction-medieval</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22223147-ozymandias?shelf=fiction-english">fiction-english</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22223147-ozymandias?shelf=fiction-french">fiction-french</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3328236382" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6835094755277538978"><b>A Brutal, Gripping Novel With A Slow Start</b><br/><br/>This is a very hard book to assess. It’s one of those stories that doesn’t really know how to begin, but once it does it lights a fire that keeps burning well after it’s over.<br/><br/>Let me explain what I mean. The opening of the book revolves around a plot to prove that the princes’ wives are adulterers by a convoluted scheme conceived by the Queen of England involving a pair of purses. The two princesses are to be given these as a gift and when they pass them </span>
  <span id="freeText6835094755277538978" style="display:none"><b>A Brutal, Gripping Novel With A Slow Start</b><br /><br />This is a very hard book to assess. It’s one of those stories that doesn’t really know how to begin, but once it does it lights a fire that keeps burning well after it’s over.<br /><br />Let me explain what I mean. The opening of the book revolves around a plot to prove that the princes’ wives are adulterers by a convoluted scheme conceived by the Queen of England involving a pair of purses. The two princesses are to be given these as a gift and when they pass them onto their lovers the plotters will identify them and out them.<br /><br />Oh, and also the Grand Master of the Knights Templar curses the king and his line into the thirteenth generation as he’s roasted on the stake as part of the royal eradication of that order.<br /><br />Now why isn’t <i>that</i> the hook rather than the purses plot?<br /><br />Each chapter takes place over a narrow period of time, usually only a few minutes. It’s designed to convey a sense of immediacy, but, especially in the early stages of the book, it also makes the story seem petty and insignificant. To compensate for this, the book is filled with ominous and rather ponderous foreshadowing. It feels unnecessary and was enough to convince me the book was going to be underwhelming. But once enough background is established and the plots start to pay off things really pick up. The last two parts are fast paced and engaging and go a long way to making up for the opening.<br /><br />Most of the characters are very complicated, although they really don’t seem so at first. Valois, for example, seems a very typical braggart knight. And yet while his conviction that every disaster comes from a failure to uphold chivalry is genuine, he’s perfectly capable of unchivalrously plotting against his own nephews without seeming like a betrayal of his character. Philip the Fair is probably most complicated of all. He’s not really an evil man, but he is a thoroughly amoral one. Cold and dispassionate with thoughts no one can read, he starts to reveal a more human side as things cease going his way. After all, while he’s killed Jews, Templars, and bankers solely to acquire their money, he’s also freed many serfs and established the first Estates General. It would be all too easy to leave him as a monster, but we have to face up to the fact that man’s character is mixed, and few indeed can be pure hero or villain.<br /><br />The book’s also very accurate. So accurate in fact, that it’s filled with footnotes of historical detail. I kind of like that, but it surprised me to find that in a book that reads so quickly and lightly.<br /><br />I have to say, I was astonished to see it was written in 1955. This feels like a much more modern book, with its frank depiction of power politics, sexuality, unsentimental pragmatism, and, yes, torture porn violence. I suppose that last one has definite Nazi parallels in mind. This was one of the inspirations for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13496.A_Game_of_Thrones__A_Song_of_Ice_and_Fire___1_" title="A Game of Thrones (A Song of Ice and Fire, #1) by George R.R. Martin" rel="nofollow noopener">Game of Thrones</a>, and it certainly shares a similar style and focus. The core of the book is power politics and the extent that men and women will go to to gain power. It doesn’t have Thrones’ fantasy elements (apart from the Templar curse) or the careful exploration of different power bases (it’s limited by real events) but it is very much of the same vein when it comes to low cunning and treachery. If you like those books and are looking for something in a more grounded format these books will likely be for you. It’s a slow start, but if you keep with it you’ll find your patience rewarded. And since most of the exposition and character setup has been got out of the way I imagine the next novels will jump right into the thick of it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6835094755277538978" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_892527858" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/892527858" />
    <a title="Terence" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1019174-terence"><img alt="Terence" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1555890512p2/1019174.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/892527858?book_show_action=true">Mar 26, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Terence" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Terence" href="/user/show/1019174-terence">Terence</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1019174-terence?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer892527858" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12355286838483709828">“This is the original <i>Game of Thrones</i>,” or so says the man who would know, George R.R. Martin, and <i>The Iron King</i> certainly has more than its share of murder, adultery, conspiracy, star-crossed lovers and bloody-minded cruelty. The only thing it doesn’t have is dragons (unless you count the ones on heraldic devices). It’s an account of the last days of the Capetian dynasty of France, when the feudal society of the Middle Ages was giving way to the modern state, and England and France became locke</span>
  <span id="freeText12355286838483709828" style="display:none">“This is the original <i>Game of Thrones</i>,” or so says the man who would know, George R.R. Martin, and <i>The Iron King</i> certainly has more than its share of murder, adultery, conspiracy, star-crossed lovers and bloody-minded cruelty. The only thing it doesn’t have is dragons (unless you count the ones on heraldic devices). It’s an account of the last days of the Capetian dynasty of France, when the feudal society of the Middle Ages was giving way to the modern state, and England and France became locked in the deadly embrace of the Hundred Years’ War.<br /><br /><i>The Iron King</i> opens a generation before the war, in 1314, when Philip the Fair successfully concludes his persecution and destruction of the Knights Templar, one of the most powerful organizations in Europe. On his pyre, its last Grandmaster, Jacques de Molay, curses the Capetians unto the 13th generation. (And, within a year, all three architects of the Templars’ fall would be dead. Coincidence? Well…yes. The curse is the stuff of urban legend; and does it really make sense that a man brutally tortured for seven years and being burned alive would have the presence of mind to enunciate a curse against his tormentors? But it does make for a good story.) Between the death of de Molay and Philip, the royal family is torn apart by adultery. The wives of the king’s three sons are implicated in affairs. Two are condemned to convents, and the third is put under house arrest (she hadn’t had a lover but she helped the others conceal the trysts), and the hapless lovers are tortured and brutally executed. Meanwhile, the king’s daughter, wife of Edward II of England, is taking advantage of the situation to put herself and her young son (future Edward III and instigator of the Hundred Years’ War) in a position to claim the crown of France.<br /><br />I would love to recommend the book wholeheartedly but I cannot. The translation is not very good. It reads like a school exercise. Something I’d expect from a student in a (admittedly advanced) French class. It competently translates the French, I’m sure, but that’s all it does – there’s no life in it. Times like this I wish my grad-school French was up to reading the original.<br /><br />Nevertheless, I’m interested enough in the story – and the translation <i>does</i> on occasion rise to the level of excellence the story deserves – that I’ll persevere through the 2nd book – <i>The Strangled Queen</i> – at the very least.<br /><br />* As an aside: One of my favorite books about the period (the 14th century) and one I’d eagerly recommend is Barbara Tuchman’s <i>A Distant Mirror</i>. If a bit dated, it brings the period to life by following the life and career of one of France’s premier – if now obscure – nobles, Enguerrand de Coucy, who dies a prisoner of the Turks in 1396 (if I recall correctly).</span>
  <a data-text-id="12355286838483709828" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_615091350" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/615091350" />
    <a title="Sarah u" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7810988-sarah-u"><img alt="Sarah u" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514831559p2/7810988.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/615091350?book_show_action=true">May 14, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah u" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah u" href="/user/show/7810988-sarah-u">Sarah u</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007491261" href="/book/show/27999638-the-iron-king">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7810988-sarah-u?shelf=france">france</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7810988-sarah-u?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7810988-sarah-u?shelf=medieval">medieval</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer615091350" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12190072854934256666">The Iron King is the first in the series of novels known as The Accursed Kings, originally written in French by Maurice Druon in 1955. Dubbed by George R.R. Martin as 'the original Game of Thrones', they have recently been translated into English by Humphrey Hare and are being re-released by Harper books.<br/><br/>I have to confess something. I bought this book because I liked the cover. That's it. They say you shouldn't judge a book by its cover, but with this one I did.<br/><br/>Thankfully, I really enjoyed this </span>
  <span id="freeText12190072854934256666" style="display:none">The Iron King is the first in the series of novels known as The Accursed Kings, originally written in French by Maurice Druon in 1955. Dubbed by George R.R. Martin as 'the original Game of Thrones', they have recently been translated into English by Humphrey Hare and are being re-released by Harper books.<br /><br />I have to confess something. I bought this book because I liked the cover. That's it. They say you shouldn't judge a book by its cover, but with this one I did.<br /><br />Thankfully, I really enjoyed this story. It opens with the end of the Knights Templar, and follows Philip the Fair of France and the events in his court throughout 1314. The story was gripping, the writing solid and I was very quickly drawn in. The fleshing out of the characters was well done and the story had everything- sex, scandal, violence and intrigue- and none of it made up. Wow.<br /><br />I did find, however, that the narrative was often punctured with what can only be described as information dumps, which were a little distracting. There were also a couple of times where the translation into English was not quite right- a baker using flower instead of flour, for example. On the whole though, these were minor issues and I enjoyed the story very much. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12190072854934256666" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3254858757" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer10895806352387528532">I read this many years ago in Hungarian and loved it. I finally got it in English and it is still the riveting story I remembered. I can’t believe this intrigue is historically accurate! While factual, Druon does introduce the suggestion of the supernatural - was it just coincidence, or was that the curse of the Grandmaster of the Templars that led to a quick ruin of Philippe the Fair and his house? <br/><br/>The action is non-stop, in fact I was missing a bit of a respite for some character development. </span>
  <span id="freeText10895806352387528532" style="display:none">I read this many years ago in Hungarian and loved it. I finally got it in English and it is still the riveting story I remembered. I can’t believe this intrigue is historically accurate! While factual, Druon does introduce the suggestion of the supernatural - was it just coincidence, or was that the curse of the Grandmaster of the Templars that led to a quick ruin of Philippe the Fair and his house? <br /><br />The action is non-stop, in fact I was missing a bit of a respite for some character development. We do get it, but in scenes that are always important to the story. I also am a bit disappointed in the writing. I am guessing that either I did not care so much 25 years ago, or that the Hungarian translation was better than the English one. The writing is adequate, just seems somewhat unsophisticated. Still, I give it five stars because the story is great and it is hard yo put down.<br /><br />This is only the intro to the series - onto the next one.</span>

<div id="review_2230845089" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2230845089" />
    <a title="Louise" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9281934-louise"><img alt="Louise" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1336194494p2/9281934.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2230845089?book_show_action=true">Dec 29, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Louise" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Louise" href="/user/show/9281934-louise">Louise</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/17566864-the-iron-king">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9281934-louise?shelf=biographical-fiction">biographical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9281934-louise?shelf=france-fic-lit">france-fic-lit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2230845089" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3428639556611695352">This is a fictional treatment of Philip IV of France. I read it to get some perspective his persecution of the Templars. It was a short book and I got a flavor for the times and a bit about the Templars. <br/><br/>As a novel I found it wanting. The book is basically 3 stories that are are not well tied together; neither are some of the episodes within them. While the main character is not developed, what is really missing from this book is “why”. <br/><br/>It begins with the persecution of the Templars which is tol</span>
  <span id="freeText3428639556611695352" style="display:none">This is a fictional treatment of Philip IV of France. I read it to get some perspective his persecution of the Templars. It was a short book and I got a flavor for the times and a bit about the Templars. <br /><br />As a novel I found it wanting. The book is basically 3 stories that are are not well tied together; neither are some of the episodes within them. While the main character is not developed, what is really missing from this book is “why”. <br /><br />It begins with the persecution of the Templars which is told to be 7 years in the making. There is a lot on the suffering of the Grand Master. The greed of Philip is mentioned, but it isn’t demonstrated. You fill in, that he must be a monster, but there are other scenes showing a humane side, for instance a late mention of his having allowed serfs to buy their freedom (quite progressive for its time.)<br /><br />The next story line is about the 3 wives of Philip’s sons. Two are entrapped in a sting designed to reveal their affairs. The third is considered an abettor. The details of the entrapment are sketchy and you go a lot on bits of info. Artois is seeking revenge for loss of his wealth (status? both?). When the target of his rage is finally revealed there isn’t enough information to justify the risk he took and the damage he caused. <br /><br />The third story line is about the Italian bankers who are blackmailing/extorting French officials.<br /><br />There are loose ends all over. When the Pope dies, there is talk of controlling the conclave, but there is nothing about why (the Templars are gone) and what they actually did. What of the young Guccio? The author says he is in love with Marie, but then he says he hardly thought of her in his absence. What of the daughters-in-law? Their story is just dropped.<br /><br />Even for being the first book of a trilogy, it ends inconclusively. No threads are tied.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3428639556611695352" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7364610-becky?shelf=in-translation">in-translation</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7364610-becky?shelf=in-my-house">in-my-house</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7364610-becky?shelf=hist-fiction">hist-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer432879690" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11265797470093186204">I can see why George RR Martin has chosen to call this the original Game of Thrones, obviously the history of the Hundred Years War can be seen as a partial inspiration for the title of his first book in the Song of Ice and Fire series. However this first book from Maurice Druon's series makes for a more laboured read. I'm not sure if it is the translation that is the issue with it, but I thought that it fluctuated between rather florid and rather dry styles. The period in which it was written m</span>
  <span id="freeText11265797470093186204" style="display:none">I can see why George RR Martin has chosen to call this the original Game of Thrones, obviously the history of the Hundred Years War can be seen as a partial inspiration for the title of his first book in the Song of Ice and Fire series. However this first book from Maurice Druon's series makes for a more laboured read. I'm not sure if it is the translation that is the issue with it, but I thought that it fluctuated between rather florid and rather dry styles. The period in which it was written may be the point here. The story is excellent, the collapse of the Templar order, and family rivalry between the daughter and daughters-in law of the French king all make for a very good story indeed. I did find that this was marred somewhat by the factual asides that dotted the text though; I thought that these detracted from the story at times. I have a reasonable knowledge of the period, so for the most part they were unnecessary hindrences for me, but even when they were useful I found them a distraction from the action of the story itself. I feel they could have been worked into the story a little better, and that at times, they made it a harder read than it needed to be. Having said that, there is plenty here to draw the reader in, and I will certainly read the translations of the other books in the series, maybe I will even test my Frech one day and tackle the original. Worth a look for any medievalist.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11265797470093186204" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_590205126" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/590205126" />
    <a title="Jason Golomb" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3213193-jason-golomb"><img alt="Jason Golomb" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1327330122p2/3213193.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/590205126?book_show_action=true">Apr 14, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jason Golomb" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jason Golomb" href="/user/show/3213193-jason-golomb">Jason Golomb</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3213193-jason-golomb?shelf=history">history</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3213193-jason-golomb?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3213193-jason-golomb?shelf=italy">italy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3213193-jason-golomb?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3213193-jason-golomb?shelf=epic">epic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3213193-jason-golomb?shelf=medieval">medieval</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3213193-jason-golomb?shelf=england">england</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer590205126" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13014268327338313415">"History is a novel that has been lived, a novel is history that could have been."<br/>E. & J. DE Goncourt<br/><br/>A few months ago, I decided to re-read George RR Martin's wonderful "A Song of Ice and Fire" series. I wanted to catch up with his amazingly flawed characters, foibles and all, remind myself of the primary plots, and catch the myriad of subplots that I missed the first time around. I got through "Game of Thrones" and "Clash of Kings" before I needed to take a little breather. <br/><br/>I poked around the i</span>
  <span id="freeText13014268327338313415" style="display:none">"History is a novel that has been lived, a novel is history that could have been."<br />E. &amp; J. DE Goncourt<br /><br />A few months ago, I decided to re-read George RR Martin's wonderful "A Song of Ice and Fire" series. I wanted to catch up with his amazingly flawed characters, foibles and all, remind myself of the primary plots, and catch the myriad of subplots that I missed the first time around. I got through "Game of Thrones" and "Clash of Kings" before I needed to take a little breather. <br /><br />I poked around the internet to see what I could find that would be similar to Martin's series. It turns out that I'm not a huge fan of fantasy. Tales of magic and cure-all potions and tricks just don't do it for me. It works in "ASOIF" because it doesn't overwhelm, and where it's prevalent, it's mythologic in scope, without impacting the detailed realism of Martin's characters. <br /><br />Then I saw on Martin's blog a reference to Maurice Duron's "The Iron King", as a seminally influential work from Martin's youth. Sadly, it was not then available in English. A near miss, but I kept my eyes open.<br /><br />And then I saw that Duron's full series, called "The Accursed Kings" would be re-released (by Martin's own publisher) in its entirety and...in English!<br /><br />I jumped at the opportunity to grab this through Amazon's Vine Program. <br /><br />And it didn't dissapoint. The first in Duron's series is called "The Iron King", focusing on a short, but influential, period in the early 14th century during the reign of French King, Philip the Fair. The first 30 pages are dense with names (a lot of princes, priests and kings of the time all had the same name) and relationships, but the story gains strength as the character qualities builds, and the plot develops. And this isn't fantasy, this is pure historical fiction...which is really what Martin created with ASOIF, except he did it in a made up world with dragons.<br /><br />"The Iron Kings" reads like an evolutionary fore-bearer to ASOIF. Superficially, many of the plot points are similar: adultery, palace intrigue, evil arbiters of the king's justice, a mix of good and bad princes and princesses, and many a-character with cliche-busting personalities. There's even a tiny bit of magic, or at least what passed for magic during the late Middle Ages. It's the realism of the human characters, though, that hints at Martin's world of kings, swords, and witty dwarves. You'll also happily recognize the persistently serious and dark themes, as well as tone throughout the story.<br /><br />The first book is just over 300 pages, but the plotting and character development are so strong, it makes for an all-too-quick read. While it's self contained as a stand-along novel, I suspect modern-day publishers would've easily combined the first several books to enable Martin-style world building on a larger scale. My biggest disappointment is that I didn't have the second in the series to read right away.<br /><br />I received this book through the Amazon Vine Program.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13014268327338313415" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('6hasBnlQRl4ZH6RuXP4ISZuVXruGS4uAQ7aSWmDcsqkFxVck3B7UvLQVCjJKwo+Px/7ZA9RpM345GG3rG54c9A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('i+nbrl4UBO/sG683BbzI/TNfmzcn/l5NS6pK+wep8lFkOiCM+1qWDUERAWsTgE87bzQcj3Xc5rMxBLVKfOtcDA==')})
  }
//]]>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer14918378011419740202">Maurice Druon was born in Paris. He is the nephew of the writer Joseph Kessel, with whom he wrote the Chant des Partisans, which, with music composed by Anna Marly, was used as an anthem by the French Resistance during the Second World War.<br/><br/>In 1948 he received the Prix Goncourt for his novel Les grandes familles. On December 8, 1966, he was elected to the 30th seat of the Académie française, succee</span>
  <span id="freeText14918378011419740202" style="display:none">Maurice Druon was born in Paris. He is the nephew of the writer Joseph Kessel, with whom he wrote the Chant des Partisans, which, with music composed by Anna Marly, was used as an anthem by the French Resistance during the Second World War.<br /><br />In 1948 he received the Prix Goncourt for his novel Les grandes familles. On December 8, 1966, he was elected to the 30th seat of the Académie française, succeeding Georges Duhamel.<br /><br />While his scholarly writing earned him a seat at the Académie, he is best known for a series of seven historical novels published in the 1950s under the title Les Rois Maudits (The Accursed Kings).<br /><br />He was Minister of Cultural Affairs in 1973 and 1974 in Pierre Messmer's cabinet, and a deputy of Paris from 1978 to 1981.<br /><br />Source: <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maurice_Druon" rel="nofollow noopener">Wikipedia</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="14918378011419740202" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
